    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="review_1812632919" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1812632919" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1812632919?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1812632919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14918715285591722141"><b>hitting<br/>enter<br/>after<br/>every <br/>word<br/>does <br/>not <br/>make<br/>it <br/>poetry.</b><br/><br/>Or maybe it does these days. Between the highly praised <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7012565.Lang_Leav' title='Lang Leav' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lang Leav</a> and this latest Goodreads Choice finalist, I guess these emo tumblr quotes are the modern version of poetry. <br/><br/>Call me old school, but I kind of expect something more. Some of these sentences are nice, sure, and some of them tickle the inner emo that lives inside us all, the one that occasionally makes us stay up late sobbing over Elliott Smith songs (oh wait, that's just me?) but co</span>
  <span id="freeText14918715285591722141" style="display:none"><b>hitting<br />enter<br />after<br />every <br />word<br />does <br />not <br />make<br />it <br />poetry.</b><br /><br />Or maybe it does these days. Between the highly praised <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7012565.Lang_Leav" title="Lang Leav" rel="nofollow noopener">Lang Leav</a> and this latest Goodreads Choice finalist, I guess these emo tumblr quotes are the modern version of poetry. <br /><br />Call me old school, but I kind of expect something more. Some of these sentences are nice, sure, and some of them tickle the inner emo that lives inside us all, the one that occasionally makes us stay up late sobbing over Elliott Smith songs (oh wait, that's just me?) but come on, is this really the best we have to offer up nowadays? At a time when we just lost the wonderful Leonard Cohen, I can't help feeling sad at the direction poetry is moving in. <br /><br />Consider these by Cohen:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Ring the bells that still can ring<br />Forget your perfect offering<br />There is a crack in everything<br />That's how the light gets in.<br /><br />Now I've heard there was a secret chord<br />That David played, and it pleased the Lord<br />But you don't really care for music, do you?<br />It goes like this<br />The fourth, the fifth<br />The minor fall, the major lift<br />The baffled king composing Hallelujah.</i>
</blockquote><br />And then this:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>the princess <br /> jumped from <br /> the tower <br /> &amp; she <br /> learned <br /> that she <br /> could fly <br /> all along.</i>
</blockquote><br />How is that even a poem? It's just a badly-punctuated sentence that sounds kinda cool. Put it in a pretty cursive font and it would get so many reblogs on tumblr. <br /><br />If you came here because, like me, you thought the whole feminist aspect sounded really interesting, I recommend you check out the witty and darkly comical <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20483085.Poisoned_Apples_Poems_for_You__My_Pretty" title="Poisoned Apples Poems for You, My Pretty by Christine Heppermann" rel="nofollow noopener">Poisoned Apples: Poems for You, My Pretty</a> instead.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14918715285591722141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3176777331939422753">Art is a pretty subjective thing, though. Everyone views it differently, there is no right or wrong way to write a poem. Personally I loved the style </span>
  <span id="freeText3176777331939422753" style="display:none">Art is a pretty subjective thing, though. Everyone views it differently, there is no right or wrong way to write a poem. Personally I loved the style and have decided to take up on a similar style, myself (I write poetry, too, and am currently majoring in English). People are quite simple and I feel they can connect and relate to this kind of poetry easier than poetry that is overly structured or more structured than this. Don't get it confused, I understand your viewpoint and respect it completely. In my opinion, however, I see nothing wrong with the structure or style they chose :)</span>

<div id="review_1839748849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1839748849" />
    <a title="Gillian Berry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13535966-gillian-berry"><img alt="Gillian Berry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354328337p2/13535966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1839748849?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gillian Berry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gillian Berry" href="/user/show/13535966-gillian-berry">Gillian Berry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32942666-the-princess-saves-herself-in-this-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=great-shelf-of-meh">great-shelf-of-meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=would-you-like-some-cheese-with-tha">would-you-like-some-cheese-with-tha</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=this-is-not-how-you-book">this-is-not-how-you-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=e-galleys">e-galleys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=poetry-and-verse">poetry-and-verse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1839748849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15077015244406916224"><br/>Okay. Yeah. That was....well, not my favorite ever thing. I feel like I just read my middle school AIM away messages or 200 pages of emo Myspace updates. I need to go listen to some Dashboard Confessional STAT.<br/><br/>I love the idea. I love the sentiments and the lessons, and CERTAINLY the feminist ideas at work here. If I saw any of the platitudes expressed in the "you" section on Tumblr, I'd happily reblog them. I definitely appreciate the raw emotions that very clearly went into the writing of them,</span>
  <span id="freeText15077015244406916224" style="display:none"><br />Okay. Yeah. That was....well, not my favorite ever thing. I feel like I just read my middle school AIM away messages or 200 pages of emo Myspace updates. I need to go listen to some Dashboard Confessional STAT.<br /><br />I love the idea. I love the sentiments and the lessons, and CERTAINLY the feminist ideas at work here. If I saw any of the platitudes expressed in the "you" section on Tumblr, I'd happily reblog them. I definitely appreciate the raw emotions that very clearly went into the writing of them, and how personal the author was willing to get about her life. BUT. Um. Ummmmmmmmm. What the fuck.<br /><br />But that...well. That's just not the kind of poetry I respond to. I find minimalist poetry EXTREMELY hit or miss, and when I (VERY RARELY) read poetry, it's usual the lusher, more ornate kind--or at least the more visually creative. Because this...I mean, there's nothing new here. It's generic Tumblr platitudes. It's emo angst that should be emblazoned over a picture of a sad girl on the beach and put on Pinterest. It's beyond basic metaphors and cliche imagery about hearts and stars and oceans. It's<br /><br />hitting <br />enter<br />after nearly<br />e v e r y <br />w o r d<br />and<br />m<br />a<br />k<br />i<br />n<br />g<br />it<br />feel<br />deep.<br /><br />To me that's just a waste of trees, but hey, to each their own.<br /><br />Again, i APPRECIATE the raw angst here, but it's pretty clunky. There's no subtlety or nuance, which is why it makes me think of 13 year old me, just scribbling out PURE FEELINGS to the page because it was the only person who'd listen and all the feelings FELT SO NEW. Which, I mean, thank you for the nostalgia, if that's what was intended, but as a book of POETRY--sophisticated poetry for the modern feminist--it's a hard pass. I mean, this book of poetry even touched on things that are very personal to me, like grief, but I got zero feels. It was all so distant and buried in cliches. <br /><br />Examples:<br /><br /><i> everyone i love leaves.</i><br /><br />I...what? What Peyton Sawyer bullshit is this? That's the whole poem?? ONE TREE HILL WAS WANGSTING LIKE THIS TEN YEARS AGO.<br /><br /><i>i hope you<br />treat her better<br />than you<br />ever<br />treated me.</i><br /><br />Did you carve this on the door of a bathroom stall or<br /><br /><i>he loves me.<br />he loves me not.<br /><br />he loves her.<br />he loves her not.<br /><br />he loves me.<br />he loves me not.<br /><br />he loves her.<br />he loves her not.<br /><br />he loves me.<br />he loves me not.<br /><br />he loves her.<br />he loves her not.<br /><br />he loves me.<br />he loves me not.<br /><br />he loves her.<br />he loves her not.<br /><br />he loves me.<br />he loves me not.<br /><br />- i ran out of petals.</i><br /><br />And I ran out of fucks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15077015244406916224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1686151272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1686151272" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <span id="freeText4194800378225630724" style="display:none"><b>"when i had<br />no friends<br />i reached inside<br />my beloved<br />books<br />&amp; sculpted some<br />out of<br />12 pt<br />times new roman</b><br /><br />-<i>&amp; it was almost good enough"</i><br /><br />I've been eyeing this book for quite a while now. I saw it on GR and Instagram and tumblr - so often, that I finally made the decision to buy it. I should give myself a high five for that. It only took one single page (the dedication) for me, an undying Potterhead, to fall in love with this beautiful collection of poems. So raw, so hurting, so emotional and empowering, that's what words are made for. This book teaches self-love and -respect, it teaches how to be strong and unapologetic, and that your life is to be written by your own quill, not by anybody else's.<br />By the way, here is the dedication:<br /><br /><i>for the boy who lived.<br />thank you for inspiring me to be<br />the girl who survived.<br />you may have<br />a lightning bolt<br />to show for it<br />but my body is a<br />lightning storm.</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="( ͡❛ _⦣ ͡❛)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="( ͡❛ _⦣ ͡❛)" href="/user/show/7249955">( ͡❛ _⦣ ͡❛)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1818746398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17727286478336578291">I'm sorry (I'm actually not sorry) BUT THIS ISN'T POETRY.<br/><br/>WTF is this?<br/><br/><i>ah, life—<br/>the thing <br/>that happens<br/>to us <br/>while we're off<br/>somewhere else<br/>blowing on<br/>dandelions<br/>& wishing<br/>ourselves into<br/>the pages of<br/>our favorite<br/>fairy tales.</i><br/><br/>THIS IS A FUCKING RIP OFF OF A JOHN LENNON QUOTE. <br/><br/>I shit you the fuck not.<br/><br/>“Life is what happens to you, while you're busy making other plans.”<br/><br/>These are tumblr quotes. This book should never have been published, OR, if it was going to be published, should have been a photo album like Ki</span>
  <span id="freeText17727286478336578291" style="display:none">I'm sorry (I'm actually not sorry) BUT THIS ISN'T POETRY.<br><br>WTF is this?<br><br><i>ah, life—<br>the thing <br>that happens<br>to us <br>while we're off<br>somewhere else<br>blowing on<br>dandelions<br>&amp; wishing<br>ourselves into<br>the pages of<br>our favorite<br>fairy tales.</i><br><br>THIS IS A FUCKING RIP OFF OF A JOHN LENNON QUOTE. <br><br>I shit you the fuck not.<br><br>“Life is what happens to you, while you're busy making other plans.”<br><br>These are tumblr quotes. This book should never have been published, OR, if it was going to be published, should have been a photo album like Kim Kardashian's #SELFIE with the actual tumblr and Instagram photos with girls braiding their hair in sunsets with cursive text and sentimental bullshit overlaid on it.<br><br>This is what this book is. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479831204i/21242255.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479831204i/21242256._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479831204i/21242257.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Does anyone SERIOUSLY disagree?!<br><br>ETA: If we're going to compare minimalist poetry, Lovelace has NOTHING on Rupi Kaur. Kaur's poems are not rip offs of other people's quotes, and her words are loaded and powerful.<br><br>Lovelace's words ... wow, is her surname a pseudonym? Because her words are as sparkly and frilly as her surname. Compare this:<br><br><i>go on,<br>collect words<br>&amp; polish them up<br>until they shine<br>like starlight <br>in your palm</i><br><br>with Kaur's. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479832081i/21242368._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One is loaded and powerful, the other is frilly sparkly tumblr shit. Guess which is which?<br><br>ETA 2: (because I'm still seething this is poetry) remember MSN statuses??! THAT'S WHAT THESE THINGS ARE. They are emo one-liners that I used to write when I was 14 to fit on a fucking MSN status box to get my crush's attention.</span>

And I loved and felt everything deeply.<br/><br/>Here are</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2739173962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6180640627080758248">Sorry, but these poems were just not my cup of tea at all. I appreciate that the author has been through A LOT and I am proud of her for being brave enough to share her words. But unfortunately I couldn’t connect to her writing, I didn’t feel any kind of emotions from reading. I’m sure there are loads of young teens who will relate to these poems, but for me; I’m past the age where writing like this would affect me. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2060570403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2060570403" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2060570403?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060570403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18045970230755593056">“the pain<br/>did not<br/>make me<br/>a better person.<br/>it did not<br/>teach me not to<br/>take anything<br/>for granted.<br/>it did not<br/>teach me anything<br/>except how<br/>to be afraid<br/>to love anyone.”<br/><br/>WOW. <br/><br/>TW: Abuse, self harm, eating disorders, suicide<br/><br/>I was expecting I would never read this, and if I did, I really wouldn’t like it. In my head, it fell under the same category as Milk and Honey, which I really, really did not enjoy because to me it lacked a lot of depth, creative writing, and—well, poeticness. I started this hesitantly, but I</span>
  <span id="freeText18045970230755593056" style="display:none">“the pain<br />did not<br />make me<br />a better person.<br />it did not<br />teach me not to<br />take anything<br />for granted.<br />it did not<br />teach me anything<br />except how<br />to be afraid<br />to love anyone.”<br /><br />WOW. <br /><br />TW: Abuse, self harm, eating disorders, suicide<br /><br />I was expecting I would never read this, and if I did, I really wouldn’t like it. In my head, it fell under the same category as Milk and Honey, which I really, really did not enjoy because to me it lacked a lot of depth, creative writing, and—well, poeticness. I started this hesitantly, but I can confidently say that although I gave this book an average rating, it still far surpassed my expectations and I can’t wait to get my hands on a finished copy so that I can mark my favorite poems. <br /><br />The good poems in this are REALLY good. I was driven to tears within the first few pages. I just wish there were more poems that blew me off my feet. I would say that for every poem I loved, there were 5 that I flipped right through without blinking. Many of these poems read like normal sentences, which is my biggest gripe about modern poetry books like Milk &amp; Honey. I crave poetry that has metaphor and depth and wordiness, so reading a 6 word poem that could literally just be a sentence is disappointing to me. At worst, some poems relied on typing words like t h i s to create e m p h a s i s and I didn’t read it with the intent I think it was written with. Some of her poems that included that style felt a bit cheesy and overdone, but it’s just my preference to have the words more straightforward. In short, I wasn’t a massive fan of her poetry formatting, but I respect her actual writing style. <br /><br />The format of her poems was mostly this:<br /><br />A stanza or two<br />talking about something<br />or someone<br />there’s a little <br />bit of t h i s<br />and maybe a metaphor<br /><br />-and then it ends with this little salutation thingy that adds a little summary or extra tidbit of info<br /><br />I’m not a fan. I liked the stanzas to stand by themselves. It’s a stylistic preference, but I felt like the extra last lines added nothing or, worse, took away from the depth or mystery of some of the shorter poems. I eventually figured out that I enjoy the poems way more without reading them, so I started skipping them altogether. <br /><br />the last section “you” is gorgeous in its intent. it’s giving advice about feminism and self love and confidence, but this section lacked the most punch for me. There was little imagery, metaphor, and playing with words. Out of all the section, this read most just like regular sentences with skips in the lines. Especially for advice that I hear a lot (“say no!" "don’t let a man save you!” “be strong!”), I prefer it to be packaged in an original way that transforms it into something new for me, but I wasn’t particularly impressed by most of them. <br /><br />Despite all this, I still really really really loved a lot of the poems. A definite step up from Milk &amp; Honey if you didn’t like that one but were considering trying this one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18045970230755593056" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1842379466" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1842379466" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1842379466?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1842379466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10156218122972314789"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>i didn't realize<br/><br/>that poetry could be achieved<br/><br/>by hitting the enter key &<br/><br/>then breaking up a sentence<br/><br/><br/><br/>with<br/><br/><br/><br/>a<br/><br/><br/><br/>space<br/><br/><br/><br/>who knew that all this time<br/><br/>my english teachers were wrong?<br/><br/>-<i> go to hell, robert frost</i><br/><br/><br/><br/>---<br/><br/><i> </i><br/><br/>So this is going to be a tricky review to write, because opinions have <i>really </i>diverged on this book. Looking through the reviews of THE PRINCESS SAVES HERSELF IN THIS ONE, you immediately see that some people adored this book and others found it</span>
  <span id="freeText10156218122972314789" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>i didn't realize<br><br>that poetry could be achieved<br><br>by hitting the enter key &amp;<br><br>then breaking up a sentence<br><br><br><br>with<br><br><br><br>a<br><br><br><br>space<br><br><br><br>who knew that all this time<br><br>my english teachers were wrong?<br><br>-<i> go to hell, robert frost</i><br><br><br><br>---<br><br><i> </i><br><br>So this is going to be a tricky review to write, because opinions have <i>really </i>diverged on this book. Looking through the reviews of THE PRINCESS SAVES HERSELF IN THIS ONE, you immediately see that some people adored this book and others found it deplorable. Age seems to be the dividing factor - this book is a hit with younger readers, and I think the generational gap has something to do with it. The Tweet-sized snippets of text remind me of the emo blogs that were so abundant on Xanga in 2005. That probably betrays my age, though. People in the "know" are calling it "Tumblr poetry." I can't vouch for that, though - this fogey-in-process doesn't have a Tumblr.<br><br><br><br>Anyway, Andrews McMeel is going to publish this book, and I'm sure the fact that the author won the Goodreads Choice Award for Best Poetry has something to do with this book deal. Andrews McMeel is a quirky publishing company that does a lot of novelty books, comics, cookbooks, and poetry. Since I've loved pretty much every book Andrews McMeel put out, I jumped when I saw this title appear on Netgalley. The fact that this book won the GCAs did make me more interested in reading it, even though poetry really isn't my bag, baby, and when one of my favorite publishers acquired it, that was the final painted nail on the elegantly manicured grabby hands. To my surprise I actually liked most of the "poems" in this volume, even if I can't really bring myself to call them that.<br><br><br><br>THE PRINCESS SAVES HERSELF IN THIS ONE is divided into four sections. Each one appears to address a different topic, and as far as I can tell, they are organized as such:<br><br><br><br>"the princess" is about how she grew up and came to be the person she is<br><br><br><br>"the damsel" is about suffering and how she almost lost sight of who she is<br><br><br><br>"the queen" is about healing and how she came to love who she is<br><br><br><br>"you" is directed towards the reader, and full of advice on what it means to be a human, and also a woman<br><br><br><br>There is a lot of suffering in this book, which is part of what makes it so raw. It's hard to get mad at someone who was brave enough to put their words to paper and then put that paper out into the world. We can mock how she chose to do it, but the fact of the matter is, she did it. Good for her. If writing this book helped her achieve cathartic release, as she claims at the end, then that is a good thing. If reading this helps others gain comfort through their suffering, that is also a good thing. Some of the "poems" are a little sappy, but there are also some great insights in here as well about self-harm, death, grief, rape, empowerment, feminism, and body dysmorphia.<br><br><br><br>At the end of the day, your opinion is your own. I'm not condemning the people who didn't like this book, because poetry is such a sensitive and subjective thing that is so deeply personal, expecting poetry to be universally beloved by all is ridiculous. Reading THE PRINCESS made me nostalgic about the blogs I kept as a high school student, which also got me through some angsty times. If you ever subscribed to "emo" culture, had an angsty blog, or the whole "chicken soup for the ____" phenomenon, read THE PRINCESS SAVES HERSELF IN THIS ONE. It'll warm your heart.<br><br><br><br>Thanks for the advanced reader copy Andrews McMeel/Netgalley! <br><br><br><br>3 to 3.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10156218122972314789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText230547688766190338" style="display:none">I want to review this honestly and go into the details about why I do not like this book of poetry. Every time I do though, I get attacked by random people who seem to have a fascination in seeing me die in random, and unimaginative, ways. Therefore, under duress:<br /> This book of poetry changed me. It is utterly 'brilliant' and 'should' be read by everyone. The way the author puts this piece of 'amazing' literature together is done 'incredibly' well. I 'love' how the poems flow and are in no way staggered and stop/start. A really 'A1' piece of literature which will, I am sure, be 'loved' by all.<br /> <br />Addition 6/12/2016: So this won the Goodreads award for poetry. Really? This is just a mess and shows how the vote is now a popularity contest, not about how good books actually are. If this is used as the standard of poetry nowadays, you can class this whole review as an epic. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2671075157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5956601310353725165">I am not into poetry the way I used to be when I was much younger, and I was meaning to pick up this book for a while now. I did not know what to expect but I was not prepared for all the emotions this book would bring out of me.<br/><br/>I had dealt with loss and grief in many unhealthy ways, ways I don’t believe I will ever repeat but reading these words about loss, confusion, guilt and rage… it hit home to me. I flew through this book and I read it again afterwards just to feel it again. <br/><br/>It’s a very si</span>
  <span id="freeText5956601310353725165" style="display:none">I am not into poetry the way I used to be when I was much younger, and I was meaning to pick up this book for a while now. I did not know what to expect but I was not prepared for all the emotions this book would bring out of me.<br /><br />I had dealt with loss and grief in many unhealthy ways, ways I don’t believe I will ever repeat but reading these words about loss, confusion, guilt and rage… it hit home to me. I flew through this book and I read it again afterwards just to feel it again. <br /><br />It’s a very simplistic evolution of a tragic and modern fairy tale where the little princess is forced to grow up too fast and yet not that fast to being able to take control. It was watching someone hitting her head against the wall over and over just waiting for a different outcome and to finally get to a point where that person can take all these awful experiences and turn them into something else. Something ugly and mesmerizing. <i> That was incredible. </i><br /><br />At the same time all these poems filled me with so much hope. I will cherish that forever.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5956601310353725165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12772859-mischas?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1957797226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6964033482727680335">I love poetry! However, I think that my love for poetry froze at the end of the nineteenth century. I'm not a fan of the poetry from the twentieth century and if this is how poetry looks in the twenty-first century than no, thank you very much. <br/><br/>I'm not going to say this is not poetry though my personal opinion might be different. (If you gave me one page from this and asked me if it was poetry, I would say a hard NO. But, as the author says: <br/><br/><i>a) poetry is ____________. <br/>- anything you want it to b</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6964033482727680335" style="display:none">I love poetry! However, I think that my love for poetry froze at the end of the nineteenth century. I'm not a fan of the poetry from the twentieth century and if this is how poetry looks in the twenty-first century than no, thank you very much. <br><br>I'm not going to say this is not poetry though my personal opinion might be different. (If you gave me one page from this and asked me if it was poetry, I would say a hard NO. But, as the author says: <br><br><i>a) poetry is ____________. <br>- anything you want it to be. </i> ) <br><br>So, here you have it. <br><br>However, in all honesty, I believe that when the calligrams appeared at first many probably thought that this was not poetry as well. I still do not like Calligram poetry, but I can respect it because that's crazy how much the poet has to plan to make it happen! 😲<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1545773797i/26809092.png" width="240" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And now everyone knows this one. ⬆ Maybe in hundred years, Amanda Lovelace will be perceived as the biggest poet of the twenty-first century, who knows!<br><br><br>I also sort of liked what the author was trying to say. I really liked the third part, the Queen. <br><br><i>when you choose<br>to sit upon a<br>throne<br>made up of<br>lies<br>&amp; <br>the bodies<br>of the people who<br>mistakenly thought<br>they could<br>t<br>r<br>u<br>s<br>t<br>you, <br><br>the only<br>thing left<br>to do<br>is<br><br>f<br>a<br>l<br>l. </i><br><br>However, that was about it. <br><br><i>“no” is short for “fuck off.” </i> No, is not short for anything! NO means NO and nothing else. <br><br>The story (I assume that it's the author's life story and for that, I'm sorry because it sounds terrible) however several times I had to disagree with her statements. For me, it was too much pushing her agenda, it tarnished the "poetry" and did not feel genuine. <br><br><br>To conclude, if you like it/love it, I'm happy for you. However, I will stay with my poetry from the nineteenth century or older. Because <i>for me personally</i> this is not something I perceive as poetry. <br><br>This would be 1,5/5⭐.</span>

<div id="review_2025916434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2025916434" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2025916434?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-buylist">x-buylist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2016">y-out2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=she-did-that">she-did-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-notowned">y-notowned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2025916434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3226927116600959427"><blockquote>
  <i>that is what abuse is:<br/>knowing you are <br/>going to get salt<br/>but still hoping for sugar<br/>for nineteen years.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>And so began my journey of love with this collection.</b><br/><br/>You'll notice I didn't use the beginning quote. Well, I didn't love this from the very beginning. Towards the beginning, <b>I found the formatting slightly annoying</b>. Some poems were fantastic and new and interesting, but some almost made me snort from their cheesiness. At times I feel Amanda Lovelace got so caught up in sounding profound she fo</span>
  <span id="freeText3226927116600959427" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>that is what abuse is:<br />knowing you are <br />going to get salt<br />but still hoping for sugar<br />for nineteen years.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>And so began my journey of love with this collection.</b><br /><br />You'll notice I didn't use the beginning quote. Well, I didn't love this from the very beginning. Towards the beginning, <b>I found the formatting slightly annoying</b>. Some poems were fantastic and new and interesting, but some almost made me snort from their cheesiness. At times I feel Amanda Lovelace got so caught up in sounding profound she forgot the true emotional core of her poems. For example, saying “we were crafted from ocean waves and starlight” <b>looks pretty, but means nothing when you think about it.</b><br /><br />Towards the second third, though, she hit her stride. I liked her poetry far more when it felt like a coherent stretch, a long length of feeling flowing from left to right across page after page. Her three-word poems did nothing for me. But God, some of the longer poems almost made me cry. <b>The sheer emotional weight of section II's poems is amazing.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>sticks and stones <br />never broke<br />my bones,<br />but words<br />made me<br />starve myself<br />until <br />you could<br />see all of them</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I also appreciated the <b>intersectionality</b> of the feminist themes presented here. Lovelace's poem on 183 especially made me cry, with both joy and sadness and something in between. <br /><br />VERDICT: Yes, it's not the best poetry of all time. But the emotional weight is beyond amazing. <br /><br />And one more quote!! <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>the love <br />some girls <br />have for <br />other girls <br />is <br />so gentle <br />&amp; so soft<br />&amp; so fucking <br />beautiful,<br />&amp; <br />these girls<br />deserve<br />to have<br />better stories<br />than the ones<br />where they<br />are murdered<br />because they love<br />with too much<br />of their<br />hearts.</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="3226927116600959427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Alex ☣ Deranged KittyCat ☣" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13555222-alex-deranged-kittycat"><img alt="Alex ☣ Deranged KittyCat ☣" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483783358p2/13555222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1852128989?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex ☣ Deranged KittyCat ☣" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex ☣ Deranged KittyCat ☣" href="/user/show/13555222-alex-deranged-kittycat">Alex ☣ Deranged KittyCat ☣</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32942666-the-princess-saves-herself-in-this-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13555222-alex-deranged-kittycat?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13555222-alex-deranged-kittycat?shelf=netgalleys-and-arcs">netgalleys-and-arcs</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13555222-alex-deranged-kittycat?shelf=memoirs-bios">memoirs-bios</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13555222-alex-deranged-kittycat?shelf=2016-favorites">2016-favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1852128989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6646961298539471569">I wish I could give this 5 stars. But hitting Enter after each word (or Space after each letter) does not make for poetry. It simply doesn't.<br/><br/>Other than that, <b>I love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32334098.The_Princess_Saves_Herself_in_this_One__Women_are_Some_Kind_of_Magic___1_' title='The Princess Saves Herself in this One (Women are Some Kind of Magic, #1) by Amanda Lovelace' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Princess Saves Herself in this One</a>!</b> Amanda, I understand your feelings completely. I know all about the sugar and the salt. My fingers were never slender enough. Nor were my ankles. Then I was too skinny. Then I became too fat. I was always told when getting a bad grade that I would never even get a job at sweeping floors. Then I</span>
  <span id="freeText6646961298539471569" style="display:none">I wish I could give this 5 stars. But hitting Enter after each word (or Space after each letter) does not make for poetry. It simply doesn't.<br /><br />Other than that, <b>I love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32334098.The_Princess_Saves_Herself_in_this_One__Women_are_Some_Kind_of_Magic___1_" title="The Princess Saves Herself in this One (Women are Some Kind of Magic, #1) by Amanda Lovelace" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Saves Herself in this One</a>!</b> Amanda, I understand your feelings completely. I know all about the sugar and the salt. My fingers were never slender enough. Nor were my ankles. Then I was too skinny. Then I became too fat. I was always told when getting a bad grade that I would never even get a job at sweeping floors. Then I was admonished for lacking self-confidence, for finding joy in the roles of wife and mother. I'll never please them, and no matter what anybody says, the hurt always follows you.<br /><br />Thank you for the courage to speak up your mind. I'll always treasure your book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>*I thank Amanda Lovelace, Andrews McMeel Publishing, and Netgalley for this copy in exchange for an honest review.</i>
</b></span>

I’m not usually into poetry. Yes, I’ve always found it quite intriguing and fantastical how a few short rightly placed words could hold such powerful and deep message. How a few short rightly placed words can create a world and a galaxy and a universe of unlimited possibilities. How a few short rightly placed words can evoke emotions of sadness, love, anger, or happiness. <br/><br/>But I decided to give this book of poetry and try</span>
  <span id="freeText4426444315697365921" style="display:none"><br>I did not<br>intend to read <br>this book <br>but<br>somehow<br>I did <br>and <br>I fell in love<br><br>So. . . I’m not usually into poetry. Yes, I’ve always found it quite intriguing and fantastical how a few short rightly placed words could hold such powerful and deep message. How a few short rightly placed words can create a world and a galaxy and a universe of unlimited possibilities. How a few short rightly placed words can evoke emotions of sadness, love, anger, or happiness. <br><br>But I decided to give this book of poetry and try and this was so much more than I anticipated. <br><br><i> Sadness, power, anger, tears, love, joy, growth, hate, </i> this book of poems is so wonderfully constructed. The story that it tells of the princess and her journey is expressed through short excerpts and it is truly magnificent.<br><br>The quotes were exceptionally powerful and strong and beautiful; I don’t think I can pick a favourite. <br><br>Every page was a new tale, a new feeling, a new life. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472994315ra/20380725.gif" width="270" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> The princess<br>jumped from<br>the tower<br>&amp; she <br>learned<br>that she<br>could fly <br>all along.<br>~ she never needed those wings. </i><br><br>5 stars!!<br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer15184757763487761571">➳ <b>3 1/2 stars</b><br/><br/>The dedication. :’)<br/><br/><blockquote>for the boy who lived.<br/>thank you for inspiring me to be<br/>the girl who survived.<br/>you may have<br/>a lightning bolt<br/>to show for it,<br/>but my body is a<br/>lightning storm.<br/><br/>⚡</blockquote><br/>I’ve seen many people write <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30075802.The_Princess_Saves_Herself_in_This_One__Women_Are_Some_Kind_of_Magic___1_' title='The Princess Saves Herself in This One (Women Are Some Kind of Magic, #1) by Amanda Lovelace' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Princess Saves Herself in this One</a> off as not being “real” poetry, or “Tumblr Poetry” (used as a derogatory term)—but as someone who’s extremely critical when it comes to reading material, <b>I actually liked it</b>, and I’m surprised that it hasn’t quite reached the critical acclaim Rupi K</span>
  <span id="freeText15184757763487761571" style="display:none">➳ <b>3 1/2 stars</b><br /><br />The dedication. :’)<br /><br /><blockquote>for the boy who lived.<br />thank you for inspiring me to be<br />the girl who survived.<br />you may have<br />a lightning bolt<br />to show for it,<br />but my body is a<br />lightning storm.<br /><br />⚡</blockquote><br />I’ve seen many people write <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30075802.The_Princess_Saves_Herself_in_This_One__Women_Are_Some_Kind_of_Magic___1_" title="The Princess Saves Herself in This One (Women Are Some Kind of Magic, #1) by Amanda Lovelace" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Saves Herself in this One</a> off as not being “real” poetry, or “Tumblr Poetry” (used as a derogatory term)—but as someone who’s extremely critical when it comes to reading material, <b>I actually liked it</b>, and I’m surprised that it hasn’t quite reached the critical acclaim Rupi Kaur’s work has.<br /><br />However, no matter the merits of the claims of it being fake poetry (who’s to judge what poetry is, or isn’t, really?) I found a few poems to be really beautiful, the sentiments that were expressed to be both powerful and empowering, and also quite painful at times.<br /><br />And isn’t that what poetry is supposed to do—make you <i>feel</i>?<br /><br /><a href="https://sprinklesofdreams.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/sprinkles-dreams-19449885" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/sprinklesofdreamsx/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://sprinklesofdreams.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/sprnklsofdreams" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>

<div id="review_1762703572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1762703572" />
    <a title="Georgia Meadows" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31098396-georgia-meadows"><img alt="Georgia Meadows" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477597781p2/31098396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1762703572?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Georgia Meadows" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Georgia Meadows" href="/user/show/31098396-georgia-meadows">Georgia Meadows</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1762703572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16929863591130187916">Let me start by saying if there was a 0 star review this collection would have gotten it. Honestly feel like I've been robbed, and rarely do I have that feeling. Moral of the story, don't buy a book based on the title and Goodreads review alone, research into its content first. Here's a list of reasons why I am doing you a favour if you don't buy this book: <br/>1. If you thought you were getting a modern Sexton or Carter, based on the idea of modernised, feminist fairytale retellings you are sorely </span>
  <span id="freeText16929863591130187916" style="display:none">Let me start by saying if there was a 0 star review this collection would have gotten it. Honestly feel like I've been robbed, and rarely do I have that feeling. Moral of the story, don't buy a book based on the title and Goodreads review alone, research into its content first. Here's a list of reasons why I am doing you a favour if you don't buy this book: <br />1. If you thought you were getting a modern Sexton or Carter, based on the idea of modernised, feminist fairytale retellings you are sorely mistaken. Instead what you get is pages after pages of quite literally moaning, and the occasional one poorly written poetic line. <br />2. I'm sick of young poets thinking the ability to put you emotions down on paper makes you a good writer, unless it's done poetically (which in this collection it rarely is) you are not writing poetry, you are writing a diary. <br />3. Following on from the idea of writing a diary I want to stress to you, THAT IS WHAT YOU ARE GETTING, sorry for caps I'm still angry at the 30 minutes of my life I spent reading this 'poetry' in hope I might get a few gems out of it, I didn't. Writing about your life and it's depressing, teenage angst is fine when it's done creatively. This could have been knocked up by any GCSE student. <br />Now despite this very harsh review I do have one positive. The opening poem. Untitled, but linking into Harry Potter and the idea of survivors Lovelace's first poem was moving and enraptured every young, lonely teenage bookworms inner thoughts and feelings. It made me remember how much I had relied of the Wizarding World to get through bad breakups and hateful friends. <br />But that was it. If I wanted to read a teenage girls diary I could dig out my embarrassing collections from the attic boxes and become depressed over by own pre-adolescent problems, I don't need/want to do it with other people's!<br />Sorry for spelling mistakes - angry typing and the editing hasn't worked! </span>
  <a data-text-id="16929863591130187916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1845219710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845219710" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1845219710?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845219710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12058339661830625765">I told myself that I would read this poetry book very slowly, even if it meant reading only one poem a day, a week, or however long in order for me to take the time to fully appreciate the words. Obviously that didn't happen when I finished it no more than 20 minutes later from starting it. XD It wasn't a very long poetry book to begin with but I didn't expect to devour The Princess Saves Herself in this One in less than 30 mins! :P<br/><br/>I was just instantly hooked and couldn't put it down. Some of th</span>
  <span id="freeText12058339661830625765" style="display:none">I told myself that I would read this poetry book very slowly, even if it meant reading only one poem a day, a week, or however long in order for me to take the time to fully appreciate the words. Obviously that didn't happen when I finished it no more than 20 minutes later from starting it. XD It wasn't a very long poetry book to begin with but I didn't expect to devour The Princess Saves Herself in this One in less than 30 mins! :P<br /><br />I was just instantly hooked and couldn't put it down. Some of them I couldn't personally relate to but they touched me anyways. Others hit so close to home that it actually made me tear up while reading. I definitely wasn't expecting that but it was good feeling being able to put your emotions into words.<br /><br />There were some poems that did feel a bit cliche and some that I've heard before in different variations because of how common those sayings already were. The Princess Saves Herself in this One is a great collection of short poems but they weren't exactly the best I've came across. Still, I enjoyed some of the poems a lot and related to a few of them.<br /><br />I know that some people complained about the style and the amount of spaces being used but I actually thought it was cute and creative. I know it's not the first poetry book to do so but it's the first that I've seen personally and I thought it was a nice little touch. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12058339661830625765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1864825595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5926047258563241275"><blockquote>#1: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864825595' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Princess Saves Herself in this One</a> ★★★★☆ <br/>#2: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2250269234' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Witch Doesn't Burn in this One</a> ★★★☆☆ <br/>#3: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2707157512' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Mermaid's Voice Returns in this One</a> ★★★★☆ <br/><br/><i>once upon<br/>a time,<br/>the princess<br/>rose from the ashes<br/>her dragon lovers<br/>made of her<br/>&<br/>crowned<br/>herself<br/>the<br/>motherfucking<br/>queen of<br/>herself.</i></blockquote><br/>Amanda Lovelace is another poet whose work I've admired from afar for a while thanks to the internet, but I've never actually read her work in collected form until now. Though this collection wasn't published until 2016, I felt like i</span>
  <span id="freeText5926047258563241275" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864825595" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Saves Herself in this One</a> ★★★★☆ <br />#2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2250269234" rel="nofollow noopener">The Witch Doesn't Burn in this One</a> ★★★☆☆ <br />#3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2707157512" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mermaid's Voice Returns in this One</a> ★★★★☆ <br /><br /><i>once upon<br />a time,<br />the princess<br />rose from the ashes<br />her dragon lovers<br />made of her<br />&amp;<br />crowned<br />herself<br />the<br />motherfucking<br />queen of<br />herself.</i></blockquote><br />Amanda Lovelace is another poet whose work I've admired from afar for a while thanks to the internet, but I've never actually read her work in collected form until now. Though this collection wasn't published until 2016, I felt like it was an incredible throwback to the mid- and late 2000s, for what it's worth. Does anyone else read Amanda's writing and hear MCR in the background? Just me? Anyways.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>if he was<br />my cup of tea,<br />then you are<br />my cup of<br />coffee.<br />tea simply<br />isn't<br />enough<br />for me<br />sometimes,<br />but<br />coffee<br />can get me<br />through<br />anything.</i>
</blockquote><br />I expected the side of <i>Princess</i> that covered grief, heartbreak, abuse, and healing, but I didn't expect the incredibly sweet love poetry that filled a substantial section of the book. I took it as a surprisingly profound view into the fact that, in her lows, Amanda's writing is absolutely heartbreaking, but in her highs, her love soars. I related to this thought much more strongly than I'd like to discuss here today, but let me just say that I saw a lot of myself in many of the words in these poems, and I will certainly be looking forward to her next collection.<br /><br /><b>Content warnings:</b> all of them. Seriously, this book comes with a page-long trigger warning sheet in the front, that ends with the same advice I would give you, too: "practice self-care before, during, &amp; after reading".</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8238362305357063770">i did really like this one! i found it on a list of suggestions after finishing a Rupi Kaur poetry collection and thought: "yes yes i have always wanted to try her books too". so apparently i read poetry now ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ i'm not sad!! it makes me want to write beautiful turns of phrase in my own work.<br/><br/>i do really love the style of this, the freeverse, and how she says "poetry is whatever you want it to be". totally felt that in her lines! and there is so much grief in the first pages, it was pure so</span>
  <span id="freeText8238362305357063770" style="display:none">i did really like this one! i found it on a list of suggestions after finishing a Rupi Kaur poetry collection and thought: "yes yes i have always wanted to try her books too". so apparently i read poetry now ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ i'm not sad!! it makes me want to write beautiful turns of phrase in my own work.<br /><br />i do really love the style of this, the freeverse, and how she says "poetry is whatever you want it to be". totally felt that in her lines! and there is so much grief in the first pages, it was pure sorrow, but i loved that she rebuilt herself. also messages of being proud in yourself? of smashing mirrors. of love of anyone who identifies as a woman. of being folded into pages of books and bleeding with the ink as they save you from mental illness? i love it.<br /><br />(it was also interesting reading the reviews of this. they went from "5stars i couldn't love this more and connected with it" straight to "1star this isn't poetry". i get not connecting with it!! but i don't understand how we have the right to police what is/isn't poetry.)</span>

<div id="review_1852574255" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1852574255" />
    <a title="Mai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12295071-mai"><img alt="Mai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477760638p2/12295071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1852574255?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mai" href="/user/show/12295071-mai">Mai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12295071-mai?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12295071-mai?shelf=why-did-i-jump-on-the-bandwagon">why-did-i-jump-on-the-bandwagon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12295071-mai?shelf=eread-audiobooks">eread-audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1852574255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11671485236544374657"><b>
  <u>I'm not criticizing, belittling or making fun of what the author has gone through by any means, it's just pure personal opinion of a book whose title I found to be intriguing.</u>
</b><br/><br/>I only read this book because it won the Goodreads award for Poetry, and honestly I wanted to know why, and I somehow couldn't find the reason, maybe it's me.<br/><br/>I'm gonna make this review as simple as the poems.<br/><br/><b>So, why two stars?</b><br/><br/>1. The poems were very personal that I actually felt uncomfortable, and this is not how you sho</span>
  <span id="freeText11671485236544374657" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>I'm not criticizing, belittling or making fun of what the author has gone through by any means, it's just pure personal opinion of a book whose title I found to be intriguing.</u>
</b><br /><br />I only read this book because it won the Goodreads award for Poetry, and honestly I wanted to know why, and I somehow couldn't find the reason, maybe it's me.<br /><br />I'm gonna make this review as simple as the poems.<br /><br /><b>So, why two stars?</b><br /><br />1. The poems were very personal that I actually felt uncomfortable, and this is not how you should feel while reading.<br /><br />2. I tried reading them out loud, and my brother thought I was mimicking Siri.<br /><br />3. I thought modern poetry is written in sentences. But then I was hit with the fact that no, it can also be written in one word per line form. Even some extremes as one letter per line.<br /><br />"it is strange<br />how<br /><br />s<br />i<br />s<br />t<br />e<br />r<br />s<br /><br />can<br />be<br /><br />s<br />a<br />v<br />i<br />o<br />r<br />s<br /><br />or<br /><br />s<br />t<br />r<br />a<br />n<br />g<br />e<br />r<br />s<br /><br />&amp;<br />sometimes<br />a bit of both.<br /><br />- <i>sisters</i>"<br /><br />How do you read that?<br /><br />4. It could've been a bit tolerable if these poems were just normal texts on tumblr. I would reblog this many times!<br /><br />5. I don't see the literature? Where's the literature? Poetry is supposed to make you feel something, and when it does then it's literature, and if it's literature then it's talent. So?<br /><br />6. I finished this book in a matter of 36 minutes, and I spent another 36 minutes searching for other alternatives of the modern poetry that I know. Also I hate when I finish books so fast, but it was that simple. Too simple.<br /><br />7. The princess didn't save herself anyway. It was just angst all over, I love reading angst, but this was a bit strange and jumping from a topic to another to the point where I got a headache.<br /><br />8. This one here is all me. I promised myself that I won't read any more free verse modern poetry but, I couldn't resist when it has a title like that. You know you have to read it. And I had high hopes.<br /><br /><b>So, why two stars?</b><br /><br />1. The title.<br /><br />2. The pain the author had to go through while writing this. It's spilled all over the pages.<br /><br /><br />This is a written note for myself to not read any more free verse modern poetry again because it's not my thing and authors invest time in writing these poems for people who actually do like it, so I don't have to waste mine reading something that isn't for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11671485236544374657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35606560-the-sun-and-her-flowers"><img alt="The Sun and Her Flowers" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1499791446l/35606560._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oSaClUI5O1K9OirhpsUw8qWki/1JLoEXSGnx2LBgCMHetJOCNwCHWESjGmsqzKKZG+DAx3UYVGhTbOdfU3NT5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lfaKvZAYA+W5GWHqG17NaaAjc2WiJooCmAfK6ReMh97qZJuq5SG/70CAUWCXV18CHmc4X54QX32DAtxu9J/c+Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Side B holds the &quot;remixes&quot; of these poems, in the form of blackout poetry, also known as &quot;found poetry.&quot; Side B gives the material a fresh twist by creating new poetry out of Side A. <span id="freeTextContainer16328241874087712457">growing up a word-devourer & avid fairy tale lover, it was only natural that amanda lovelace began writing books of her own, & so she did. when she isn't reading or writing, she can be found waiting for pumpkin spice coffee to come back into season & binge-watching gilmore girls. (before you ask: team jess all the way). the lifelong poetess & storyteller currently lives in new jersey with her fian</span>
  <span id="freeText16328241874087712457" style="display:none">growing up a word-devourer &amp; avid fairy tale lover, it was only natural that amanda lovelace began writing books of her own, &amp; so she did. when she isn't reading or writing, she can be found waiting for pumpkin spice coffee to come back into season &amp; binge-watching gilmore girls. (before you ask: team jess all the way). the lifelong poetess &amp; storyteller currently lives in new jersey with her fiancé, their moody cat, &amp; a combined book collection so large it will soon need its own home. she has her B.A. in english literature with a minor in sociology. the princess saves herself in this one is her debut poetry collection &amp; the first book in the women are some kind of magic series. the second book in the series, the witch doesn't burn in this one, will be published in 2018.</span>
